### Post by ocirne94 on 2016-05-27

I have been trying to upgrade my 14.04.4 64-bit to the new 16.04, but with no luck.
I get stuck in a weird dependencies hell where core packages are broken. Here is the apt.log file generated by
$ sudo do-release-upgrade -d,
which complains "can't calculate the update" and exits:

### Post by oldos2er on 2016-05-27
Why the -d switch? That would upgrade you to yakkety 16.10. All you need is ```
do-release-upgrade
```

---

### Post by Impavidus on 2016-05-27
I've seen conflicting statements on the forums. According to some, do-release-upgrade -d will always upgrade to 16.10. According to others, it will upgrade 16.04 to 16.10, but 14.04 (for the time being) to 16.04. Without the -d option 14.04 won't upgrade at all until the release of 16.04.1 – unless set to upgrade to any version, in which case it may upgrade to 15.10, which is definitely not recommended.

Anyway, no upgrade was performed. This may be because you have incompatible third-party software. You may have to disable third-party software sources before upgrading. You may want to postpone your upgrade until the upgrade from trusty to xenial is officially supported in about two months.

---

### Post by ocirne94 on 2016-05-27
> Without the -d option 14.04 won't upgrade at all until the release of 16.04.1

Correct, that's why I am using it.

> You may have to disable third-party software sources before upgrading
I had a long list of ppas, I have used ppa-purge to revert to official packages.

### Post by Omar_Jair on 2016-05-27
Have you tried a "ppa-purge" or installing the GTK-ORPHAN package, it looks for packets with unmet dependencies so you dont have to search one by one.

### Post by UltimateCat on 2016-05-28
Sometimes a fresh installation is the best way to stop the headache of dependency hell.-:D

-::-In the time that it has taken to fix what's not right you could of already performed a fresh install.-::-

### Post by deadflowr on 2016-05-28
It might help to know the exact steps you ran that put you in the current state.
Like which apt-get commands, or what have you, were run and when.
Hopefully in the order in which they were run, as well.
